## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics / classical mechanics
**Analysis**: This task models the acceleration of a nonlinear harmonic oscillator, where dv_dt depends on position x, velocity v, and possibly time t through restoring forces, damping, and driving terms. The nonlinearity can appear in the potential (position-dependent) or dissipation (velocity-dependent) terms.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Duffing with damping and driving: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (forced damped Duffing oscillator)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * v * (1 + c1 * x**2) + c2 * x (self-excited oscillator with nonlinear damping)
- Rayleigh oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (velocity-dependent nonlinear damping)
- Damped linear oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (linear restoring + linear damping)
- Quintic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order anharmonic potential)
- Softening/hardening spring: dv_dt = c0 * x * (1 + c1 * x**2) (amplitude-dependent stiffness)
- Nonlinear damping with restoring: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v * x**2 (position-dependent damping)
- Morse-type oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * exp(c1 * x) * (1 + c2 * exp(c1 * x)) (asymmetric potential well)
- Parametric oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x * cos(c1 * t) + c2 * v (time-modulated stiffness)
- Coulomb-damped oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * (v**2)**(-0.5) (constant friction approximation via v/|v|)
- Pendulum-like: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * x) (sinusoidal restoring force)
- Cubic damping with cubic spring: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * v**3 (fully nonlinear oscillator)
- Mixed nonlinear coupling: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x * v + c2 * x**2 (position-velocity cross terms)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope ŌåÆ Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects ŌåÆ Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay ŌåÆ Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior ŌåÆ Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects ŌåÆ Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power restoring forces (x, x┬│, xŌüĄ) ŌåÆ symmetric potential wells preserving oscillator symmetry
- Velocity-dependent terms proportional to v*(1 - x┬▓) ŌåÆ limit cycle behavior (Van der Pol type self-excitation)
- Cubic position terms (x┬│) with same/opposite sign as linear term ŌåÆ hardening/softening spring nonlinearity
- Sinusoidal functions of position sin(c*x) ŌåÆ periodic potential or pendulum-like large-amplitude oscillations
- Odd functions of v (v, v┬│, v|v|) ŌåÆ dissipative terms; even functions of v (v┬▓) ŌåÆ non-dissipative nonlinear coupling
- Absence of explicit time dependence ŌåÆ autonomous system (conserved energy if also no velocity terms)
- Products x*v or x┬▓*v ŌåÆ nonlinear damping whose strength depends on displacement amplitude
- Cosine/sine of time cos(c*t) ŌåÆ external periodic driving force leading to possible resonance or chaos

Combining linear x terms: `-3.43809*x - 3.43809*x = -6.87619*x`

So GT = `-1.89975*v - 6.87619*x - 3.43809*x**3 - 0.06601*x*|v|^(1/3)`

The key terms are:
1. `v` (linear)
2. `x` (linear)
3. `x**3` (cubic)
4. `x*|v|^(1/3)` ŌĆö this is the problematic term with absolute value and fractional power of v

The term `x*|v|^(1/3)` is very distinctive. None of the candidate formulas contain `|v|` or `Abs(v)` explicitly. So I need to check if any candidate can reproduce this term through some combination.

The term `|v|^(1/3)` is a nonlinear, non-polynomial function of v that behaves differently for positive and negative v (it's even in v, like `|v|`). No polynomial combination of v (like `v`, `v**2`, `v**3`, etc.) can reproduce `|v|^(1/3)` since `|v|^(1/3)` is not differentiable at v=0 in the same way polynomials are, and it's an even function times x.

Let me check candidates with exponential or special functions that might approximate this:

**Candidates with `exp` terms (like `x*exp(c*x**2)`)**: These depend on x, not v, so they can't produce the `|v|^(1/3)` dependence.

**Candidates with `(c*x**2 + 1)**(1/3)` or `(c*x**2+1)**c`**: These involve x, not v.

**Candidate 38**: `c0*v + c1*v*x**2 + c2*x + c3*x**3 + c4*x*(c5*x**2 + 1)**c6 + c7*v*x*sin(c8*t + c9)` ŌĆö The power term is in x, not v. Can't match.

**Candidates with `log` and `exp`**: These involve x only (like `log(c*exp(c*x)+1)`), not v.

**Candidates with `cos(c*exp(c*x))`**: Again, x-dependent, not v-dependent.

None of the candidates have any term that depends on `|v|^(1/3)` or any fractional/absolute-value power of v. The v-dependent terms in all candidates are polynomial in v (like `v`, `v**2*x`, `v**3`, `v*x**2`, etc.) or involve `v` multiplied by trigonometric functions of t.

Since `x*|v|^(1/3)` is an even function of v (symmetric) and non-polynomial, no polynomial in v can replicate it. The coefficient `0.06601` is small but nonzero, and the problem states this is a physics oscillator where v takes negative values, so we cannot ignore the absolute value.

Even if we tried to approximate by setting the problematic term to zero, the GT has a specific nonzero coefficient for `x*|v|^(1/3)`, and we're checking for exact mathematical equivalence, not approximation.

No candidate can reproduce the `x*|v|^(1/3)` term.
